                            <div class="player-info-box-header "><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Rajai Davis</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team">Cleveland Indians (AAA)</div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 37</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">5' 10" / 195</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">OF</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>10/19/1980 (37 y, 4 m, 19 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=3708&position=OF#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2001 June Amateur Draft - Round: 38, Pick: 8, Overall: 1134, Team: Pittsburgh Pirates</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=3708&position=OF#contract" >$6M / 1 Years (2017)</a>
                        </div>
                    </td>

                    
                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=8387">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Davis has agreed to a minor-league deal with the Indians that includes an invitation to spring training, Jordan Bastian of MLB.com reports. (2/17/2018)</div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>A former 38th-round draft pick of the Pittsburgh Pirates, Davis transformed himself from waiver bait to the starting center fielder in Oakland. Snagged from the Giants last April, Davis flat lined at the plate in 2008. But he hit in excess of .300 in 2009, swiping 41 bases in 53 attempts. A highly aggressive hitter, Davis walked in less than 7% of his plate appearances while swinging at nearly 31% of pitches thrown outside of the strike zone. Even so, he worked the count better than in 2008, when he drew a free pass less than 4% and hacked at 36% of outside pitches. By August, Davis was a fixture in Oakland's lineup, often batting second. He played best down the stretch, with an .831 OPS in September and early October.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Davis has the wheels to steal 50-plus bases in 2010, making him a hot name in fantasy circles. But as the old baseball axiom says, “You can't steal first base.” The 5’11”, 195 pound righty batter draws few walks and rarely puts a charge into the ball, so he's highly dependent on his batting average. Davis possesses the speed to beat out infield hits and he smacks a healthy number of line drives, but his BABIP was a lofty .366 in 2009. Odds are, that number is going to dip 20 or 30 points next year. If his BABIP regresses, Davis would be more of a .270-.280 hitter instead of the .300-plus sparkplug that the A's enjoyed this past season. Davis' roadrunner act on the bases makes him a great source of steals, but don't expect him to bat .300 again. (David Golebiewski)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Rajai Davis’s position within Toronto’s outfield is unclear. It partly depends on where Jose Bautista and Travis Snider end up playing since both are ahead of him in importance to the Blue Jays. If Davis can work his way into a regular role, he becomes immediately valuable thanks to his incredibly high steal totals. Davis swiped 50 bags last year and 41 in just 125 games during 2009. Those advancements help him pad his runs-scored total as well and the infield hits have kept his batting average from falling too low. The Blue Jays being such an offensive force should translate to a goodly share of RBI opportunities as well if he can crack the lineup. Davis will not give you anything in home runs but he is worth having for his steals alone. Even as a part-time player with Toronto, he’s likely to see plenty of pinch-running chances and might amass 25-30 steals on those alone, like in 2008 when he stole 29 bases and had just 214 plate appearances. (Matthew Carruth)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Keeping an eye on Davis will be hard because of his speed, but it’s worth trying. If he slips in the draft because he lacks a starting role, he could be a cheap source of steals for you.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>A setback while recovering from a torn hamstring ended what was a very disappointing, injury-filled first year in Toronto for Rajai Davis. His .238 batting average was the lowest of his career since becoming an everyday player in 2008 with Oakland, as Davis struggled mightily against right-handed pitching, something he’d been successful at in both 2009 and 2010. The injuries took their toll on Davis’ running game, too, in which he specializes. Davis’ 34 stolen bases were a three-year low, and his stolen base percentage dropped, too. Now that he’s scheduled to be the back-up center fielder to Colby Rasmus, what little fantasy value Davis does have -- as a speedster, at the very least -- has been reduced. Davis could perhaps fill out your bench in a deeper league, maybe, but that’s about it. (Navin Vaswani)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The move from Oakland to Toronto wasn’t a smooth one for Rajai Davis, who struggled mightily in 2011. With Colby Rasmus entrenched in center field in Toronto in 2012, Davis has little fantasy value other than to swipe you a base from time to time. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Rajai Davis does one thing very well: steal bases. And that gives him some fantasy value. He stole 46 bases in 2012, in 142 games, and, re-signed to a one-year deal, he’ll be a bench player for the Blue Jays in 2013. A below-average hitter, draft Davis late, or grab him for a few dollars, and he’ll do what he does, albeit in likely a more limited role: steal between close to 30 bases while hitting mostly against left-handers or late in games as a defensive replacement. (Navin Vaswani)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If you’re looking for stolen bases on the cheap, Rajai Davis could be just the man you’re looking for. But that’s where it begins and ends: stolen bases.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Some players are more valuable in fantasy than in real baseball, and vice-versa. Rajai Davis is more valuable in fantasy, but it is not as if he is totally worthless in real baseball. And, in fact, if one just looks at his hitting line (.268/.316/.377) and his unexceptional outfield defense, he might look like a replacement-level player in both fantasy and reality. However, Davis, currently a free agent, has value beyond that. According to baserunning metrics (both base stealing and baserunning in general), in real baseball he was worth about a win above average just on the bases. In category leagues, these are the relevant numbers: 41, 50, 34, 46, 45. Those are Davis' numbers of stolen bases during the previous five seasons. He managed those 45 steals in 2013 in less than 400 plate appearances. Davis is 33, so his speed (his only asset) is probably on the decline, but even in a half-time job with Andy Dirks in Detroit's left field, he could easily steal 40 again. That means very good value in category leagues, despite Davis' lack of other contributions. (Matt Klaassen)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Davis' only asset in fantasy ball is his high number of steals, but a player who can steal 40 or more bases in part-time action has serious value in any category league.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Look over the 2014 stats for Davis, and you might conclude that he just had his career season. With a couple of injuries to the Tigers outfield, Davis became a full time player. He took advantage of the opportunity with near career highs in home runs, RBI and runs. His .282 average was his highest value since 2010, when he hit .284. His average has been improving from a low of .238 in 2011 to .282 this past season due mainly to a couple changes he's made to his approach. He has dropped his strikeout rate from around 20% to 15% by making by making more contact when he swings (77% contact percentage in 2011, up to 83%). Also, he is taking advantage of his speed by hitting the ball on the ground more -- his ground-ball rate has gone from 44% to 50%. His speed may finally be on the decline, though. His stolen base totals went from 45 in 2013 to 36 in 2014 in almost the same number of attempts (51 vs 47).  His success rate dropped from 88% to 77%. The success rate is still acceptable, but be careful if it drops even further. One issue with Davis will be playing time. Besides the newly acquired Yoenis Cespedes, the other Tiger outfielders (Anthony Gose, J.D. Martinez, Stephen Moya, and Daniel Fields) have huge questions surrounding them. Davis will probably get his 30+ steals, but it remains to be seen if he gets enough playing time to contribute in the other categories. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Rajai was a full time outfielder for the Tigers in 2014 and he had probably his best season ever. He may not be able to repeat the season because of playing time issues, and his speed dropping off. Consider him a fringe mixed leaguer. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The 35-year-old Davis is who he is at this point, and that's a decent outfielder who's probably best suited to be on the small side of a platoon. He was almost split neutral in 2015, but that's a diversion from his long standing track record of hitting lefties very well and struggling against righties. Regardless, he always seems to find his way into more playing time than those splits would suggest, receiving at least 338 plate appearances for seven consecutive seasons. He now pencils in as the Indians' leadoff bat and left fielder, and there's no clear candidate for the opposite side of the platoon. If the Indians plan to give Davis more regular run, it may hurt his batting average but would obviously stand to help his counting stats. Those are what Davis is owned for, anyway, as he's usually good for 10 home runs and 40-plus steals per-600 plate appearances, and a leadoff slot could help his runs total. There's some concern that the speed is waning, as he managed just 18 stolen bases in 26 attempts last year, but he also posted his best speed score since 2011, so it may just be noise. Watch Indians camp closely to see if Davis is running well and if the team finds a lefty to work alongside him. So long as he's moving fine, he's on the radar in deeper or AL-only formats. (Blake Murphy)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Davis saw a dip in stolen bases, but even at age 35 he's a safe speed bet. The Indians may install him in the leadoff spot, and the lack of a clear platoon partner means he could see more regular plate appearances than usual.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Rajai Davis is fast. And he is good at stealing bases. 2016 was his fifth year out of the past eight with 40 steals, and he stole 30+ in two of the other three. Davis is not all that good at anything else. His power has emerged late in his career, but he still has only 28 home runs over the last three seasons (though Aroldis Chapman will tell you, Rajai can hit a mistake). None of his rates are special. He isn't a great fielder. He does hit lefties pretty well (Chapman learned that, too), but not so well that he is worth rostering as a platoon bat. But if he plays, he a) won't kill any of your stats, and b) will steal all the bases there are to be stolen. If he ends up with a regular job and you are playing 5x5, he is a great fantasy asset. If he doesn't and/or you are not, he is not.(<a href="https://twitter.com/chadyoung">Chad Young</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Are you playing 5x5 (or another format that highly values SB)? If so, keep an eye on where Davis signs and what his role will be. He doesn't do much else, but he is a lock for 40 steals if he has a job.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
